      95             : /*!
      96             : \page gdal_api_proxy GDAL API Proxy
      97             : 
      98             : \section gdal_api_proxy_intro Introduction
      99             : 
     100             : (GDAL >= 1.10.0)
     101             : 
     102             : When dealing with some file formats, particularly the drivers relying on
     103             : third-party (potentially closed-source) libraries, it is difficult to ensure
     104             : that those third-party libraries will be robust to hostile/corrupted datasource.
     105             : 
     106             : The implemented solution is to have a (private) API_PROXY driver that will
     107             : expose a GDALClientDataset object, which will forward all the GDAL API calls to
     108             : another process ("server"), where the real driver will be effectively run. This
     109             : way, if the server aborts due to a fatal error, the calling process will be
     110             : unaffected and will report a clean error instead of aborting itself.
     111             : 
     112             : \section gdal_api_proxy_enabling How to enable ?
     113             : 
     114             : The API_PROXY mechanism can be enabled by setting the GDAL_API_PROXY config
     115             : option to YES.  The option can also be set to a list of file extensions that
     116             : must be the only ones to trigger this mechanism (e.g. GDAL_API_PROXY=ecw,sid).
     117             : 
     118             : When enabled, datasets can be handled with GDALOpen(), GDALCreate() or
     119             : GDALCreateCopy() with their nominal filename (or connection string).
     120             : 
     121             : Alternatively, the API_PROXY mechanism can be used selectively on a datasource
     122             : by prefixing its name with API_PROXY:, for example GDALOpen("API_PROXY:foo.tif",
     123             : GA_ReadOnly).
     124             : 
     125             : \section gdal_api_proxy_options Advanced options
     126             : 
     127             : For now, the server launched is the gdalserver executable on Windows. On Unix,
     128             : the default behaviour is to just fork() the current process. It is also possible
     129             : to launch the gdalserver executable by forcing GDAL_API_PROXY_SERVER=YES.  The
     130             : full filename of the gdalserver executable can also be specified in the
     131             : GDAL_API_PROXY_SERVER.
     132             : 
     133             : It is also possible to connect to a gdalserver in TCP, possibly on a remote
     134             : host. In that case, gdalserver must be launched on a host with "gdalserver
     135             : -tcpserver the_tcp_port". And the client must set
     136             : GDAL_API_PROXY_SERVER="hostname:the_tcp_port", where hostname is a string or a
     137             : IP address.
     138             : 
     139             : On Unix, gdalserver can also be launched on a Unix socket, which "gdalserver
     140             : -unixserver /a/filename".  Clients should then set GDAL_API_PROXY_SERVER to
     141             : "/a/filename".
     142             : 
     143             : In case of many dataset opening or creation, to avoid the cost of repeated
     144             : process forking, a pool of unused connections is established. Each time a
     145             : dataset is closed, the associated connection is pushed in the pool (if there's
     146             : an empty bucket). When a following dataset is to be opened, one of those
     147             : connections will be reused. This behaviour is controlled with the
     148             : GDAL_API_PROXY_CONN_POOL config option that is set to YES by default, and will
     149             : keep a maximum of 4 unused connections.  GDAL_API_PROXY_CONN_POOL can be set to
     150             : a integer value to specify the maximum number of unused connections.
     151             : 
     152             : \section gdal_api_proxy_limitations Limitations
     153             : 
     154             : Datasets stored in the memory virtual file system (/vsimem) or handled by the
     155             : MEM driver are excluded from the API Proxy mechanism.
     156             : 
     157             : Additionnaly, for GDALCreate() or GDALCreateCopy(), the VRT driver is also
     158             : excluded from that mechanism.
     159             : 
     160             : Currently, the client dataset returned is not protected by a mutex, so it is
     161             : unsafe to use it concurrently from multiple threads. However, it is safe to use
     162             : several client datasets from multiple threads.
     163             : 
     164             : \section gdal_api_proxy_concurrent Concurrent use of a dataset
     165             : 
     166             : Starting with GDAL 2.1 (Unix only), if the gdalserver executable is launched in
     167             : TCP (or Unix socket) mode, and with the -nofork flag, clients that will open the
     168             : same dataset name through the API Proxy will be associated with the same dataset
     169             : object on the server, thus enabling, for example, safe "concurrent" write from
     170             : several clients.
     171             : 
     172             : But in that mode, only one thread is used in the server, hence
     173             : reducing scalability and client isolation. Furthermore some operations, like
     174             : "gdal_translate api_proxy:in.tif api_proxy:out.tif" are not possible, since they
     175             : would deadlock the server.
     176             : 
     177             : */
     178             : 
     179             : /* REMINDER: upgrade this number when the on-wire protocol changes */
     180             : /* Note: please at least keep the version exchange protocol unchanged ! */
     181             : #define GDAL_CLIENT_SERVER_PROTOCOL_MAJOR 3
     182             : #define GDAL_CLIENT_SERVER_PROTOCOL_MINOR 0
